60	    
The strain C230 was isolated from a cooked pasta dish in another study (62), with pH= 6.6 and salt 
content at 0.9 %. The strain C230 was studied at three different growth temperatures, such as 40, 
44, and 47 °C, and obtained growth at all temperatures. Compared to the other study (62), higher 
pH (7.4) and lower salt content (0.5 %) were used in the present study. C230 belonged to the as-
sumed phylogenetic group III, which have a growth temperature range on BA-plates between 12-49 
°C, and in BHI-broth between 30-45 °C. The strain showed the same growth ability in BHI-broth 
and in Mornay sauce up to 50 °C.  
Statistical calculations were used to show the significant differences between the applied strains, 
substrates, and to show the interaction between strains and substrates. There was a significant dif-
ference on T0 between strains (p= 0.0212) at 45 °C, therefore it was required to test for log-increase 
instead of log(CFU/mL). It was completed by subtracting log(CFU/mL) for T0 from T3 and T6. It 
provides a p-value of p < 0.0039, which means, there was a significant interaction between strains 
(C230, T100, and T185) and substrates (BHI-broth, asparagus soup and Mornay sauce) and growth 
of strains were different in the different substrates. In order to interpret the results, 95 % confidence 
intervals were calculated and compared in log-increase graph.  
As the growth of the strains were different for substrates, each combination was interpreted by cal-
culating 95 % confidence intervals. Figure 15 illustrates log-increase for T3-T0.

If confidence intervals are higher than 0.5 log-increase or overlap with 0.5 log-increase, it is likely 
that the strains can grow in the substrates, such as C230 in BHI-broth, T100 in Mornay sauce and 
T185 in Mornay sauce within 3-hours of incubation at 45 °C, which corresponds to growth in table 
21.  
The log-increase graph (T6-T0) (Figure 16) for the 6-hour incubation at 45 °C shows, that there was 
not overlap between the confidence intervals, which means, growth within 6-hour for all combina-
tions, such as in BHI, asparagus soup and in Mornay sauce.

Figure 17 defines, that there was no difference in growth of Bacillus cereus sensu lato strains in the 
different substrates at 48 °C, after 6-hour incubation. Due to the overlap of confidence intervals on 
the 0.5 log-increase graph (Figure 17) it was interpreted to growth of the strains like, C230 in Mor-
nay sauce, T185 in BHI-broth and T185 in Mornay sauce within 6-hour incubation at 48 °C. Statis-
tical analyzes for this experiment, do not agree with growth results shown in Table 21, as C230 was 
defined as no-growth at 48 °C. Because of the difference between the T0 strains, which meant that 
the growth of the strains was different in the different substrates, it was required to calculate the 95 
% confidence intervals to see at each combination to interpret the results that are more correct.

Figure	  18:	  Log-­‐increase	  for	  T6-­‐T0	  to	  shows	  the	  interpret	  the	  interaction	  between	  strains	  and	  substrates	  after	  six-­‐hour	  incubation	  at	  
50	  °C.	  	  
After 6-hour hot-holding at 50 °C of substrates (asparagus soup, Mornay sauce and BHI-broth), 
which were seeded with different strains consisted of C230, T100 and T185 resulted, that there was 
no difference in the growth of the Bacillus cereus strains (Figure 18).  As seen from the Figure 18, 
growth was achieved of the strains C230 and T100 in Mornay sauce and T185 in Mornay sauce and 
in BHI-broth. There was again discrepancy of the strain C230, which shows growth in BHI-broth 
by statistical calculations, but when comparing with the growth table 21, no growth was seen, 
which may be due to the same reason as explained before below Figure 17.  
Bacillus cereus strains and substrates were significantly different (p < 0.0257) for T0 strains at 52 
°C. But, log-increase calculations both for T3-T0 showed no significant difference between sub-
strates (p > 0.6325) and strains (p > 0.0817), and interaction between strains and substrates was p > 
0.5513. The reason for different significance for T0 and T3-T0 confirms that the method used in pre-
sent study was not able to ensure, that the number of Bacillus cereus strains from start in all cases 
was the same. To get more robust results it may be necessary to make more determinations than 
two, e.g. triplicate.

64	    
The varying growth results obtained may be due to as men-
tioned previously (section Main tests in foods) the commercial 
foods (Asparagus soup and Mornay sauce) consistency, it was 
difficult to take samples of these foods with the pipette. It may 
be, that the volume of the soup and sauce was reduced, which 
made have resulted in lower counts. The second reason may 
be due to the difficulty of counting Bacillus cereus sensu lato 
colonies on TSA-plates. Because, when the TSA-plates were 
incubated at room temperature (21-22 °C), it took more than 
24 h before seeing any colonies on the plates and by incubat-
ing the TSA-plates at 30 °C, the colonies became too large 
and it was impossible to count the colonies because of inter-
growth (Figure 19). Hence, the incubation of the plates may 
only be at room temperature (21-23 °C) until the colonies grow, to get more reliable results.  
Based on the repeated experiments of testing the strains both in BHI-broth and on BA-plates, then 
by OD-measurements in water-bath showed that the growth on BA-plates were more reliable com-
pared to BHI-broth, as it showed varying growth ability already in the first BHI experiments, as it 
grew up to 55 °C. The repeated experiments in the water bath showed that the strains grew only up 
to 53 °C (T185) and 55 °C (T100).  
The purchased commercial foods (asparagus soup and Mornay sauce) used in the present study con-
tained modified starch, wheat flour, milk, cream, cheese powder, which are good growth conditions 
for Bacillus cereus sensu lato (28). Both with the pre-tests in BHI-broth and in the main-tests exper-
iments in Mornay sauce and in asparagus soup, the conclusive factor for the growth of the Bacillus 
cereus sensu lato strains was only incubation temperatures. The reason, that neither pH nor salt con-
tent has not shown any effect on the growth of the strains T185, C230 and T100 in nutrient rich 
substrates may be due to the growth characteristics of the Bacillus cereus sensu lato. The applied 
pH and salt content used in the present study are very close to each other and are within the growth 
characteristic of Bacillus cereus sensu lato. The strains T100 and T185 are in the same assumed 
phylogenetic group IV, which has the pH range between 7-4.8 (Table 1) and NaCl range between 
0.5-8 % (Table 2).

soup	  and	  incubated	  within	  6	  h	  at	  45	  ℃. 
==PAGE:66==
DTU	  National	  Food	  Institute	  Research	  Group	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  s093510	  Mehtap	  Polat	  Akyol	  	  
for	  Microbiology	  and	  Hygiene	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  Master	  Thesis	  in	  Food	  Technology	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	      
	  
	  
	  
65	    
The method conducted in this study was not reliable, as the strains did not show growth differences 
in different substrates at the different temperatures. It could give more reliable data, to make more 
determinations of the same experiments. Sampling provided also uncertainty as pipetting of the 
samples was difficult due to the consistency of foods. Instead of taking the sample with the pipette, 
which reduced the volume of the foods, it might be more useful to use a bigger pipette or spoon and 
transfer the required volume into a glass tube in a large quantity, to be sure to take the same volume 
every time.  
The experiments performed showed that growth was already achieved within 3 h incubation. As the 
samples were taken before incubation at different temperatures and subsequently 3 h and 6 h it is 
unknown, whether the Bacillus cereus sensu lato growth occurred within 3-hour incubation. If sam-
ples were taken at each hour and made a growth curve, it would give a clearer results of the growth. 
In another study, samples of RTE foods (cooked pasta) were taken within 8 h, at each hour, at dif-
ferent temperatures between 40 and 47 °C, which showed that there was growth after 2 h hot-hold-
ing at 47 °C of the strain C230 (62).  
In the present study growth was achieved up to 52 °C of the strains within 6-hour incubation. Ex-
periments in BHI-broth overnight showed that none of the selected samples C230, T100 or T185 
grew ≥ 54, therefore it is necessary to hot-hold RTE foods at ≥ 54 °C to avoid germination of the 
Bacillus cereus sensu lato spores.  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:67==
DTU	  National	  Food	  Institute	  Research	  Group	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  s093510	  Mehtap	  Polat	  Akyol	  	  
for	  Microbiology	  and	  Hygiene	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  Master	  Thesis	  in	  Food	  Technology	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	      
	  
	  
	  
66	    
Conclusion  
This project investigated the growth of Bacillus cereus sensu lato from different strains in liquid 
substrates (BHI-broth) that represented sauces and soups, to establish safe hot-holding times and/or 
temperatures.  
The growth ability of the ubiquitous bacteria, Bacillus cereus sensu lato in twenty strains, including 
isolates from different sources, as pasta, rice, soft ice, tomato, and some commercial products were 
examined. All these twenty collected strains from DTU Food were identified using MALDI-TOF 
MS. Seventeen of the strains were identified as Bacillus cereus, whereas the other three strains 
(16238, 17544 and C261) were identified with three difference suggestions of Bacillus spp. such as 
Bacillus weihenstephanensis, B. thuringiensis and Bacillus mycoides. Then, the conventional PCR 
method was used to test the presence of the six toxin genes (CES, CER, hblC, nheA, hblC and cytK) 
in all twenty Bacillus cereus sensu lato strains. The emetic toxins, such as CES and CER genes 
were present in three strains, 21792, 10329 and 17533. Nineteen of the tested strains (21750, 21792, 
21800, 16238, 10329, 11129, 21803, 21791, T101, T100, 17533, T185, T183, T126, T147, Tomato, 
C261, C230, and 21793) contained the enterotoxins entFM and nheA genes, except the strain 
17544. Ten of the tested strains (21750, 16238, 11129, 21803, 21791, T101, T100, T185, Tomato 
and 21793) contained the enterotoxin cytK gene. Lastly, the enterotoxin gene hblC were present in 
eleven strains (21750, 21800, 16238, 11129, 21803, 21791, T101, T100, T185, Tomato, and 
21793).  
To investigate the growth in liquid foods, it was necessary to select suitable strains, that could grow 
at higher temperatures to show Bacillus cereus sensu lato growth at hot-holding. Three strains 
(C230, T100 and T185) were then selected based on their growth ability at higher temperature on 
BA-plates up to 49 °C and in BHI-broth up to 53 °C. These selected strains were used for the pro-
duction of spores, in order to investigate the growth in substrates, BHI-broth, asparagus soup and in 
Mornay sauce at different temperatures 45, 48, 50, and 52 °C within six hours hot-holding. The 
growth experiments showed that strains showed growth in the applied substrates at different tem-
peratures, such as T185 grew in Mornay sauce at 45 °C and in BHI-broth at 45, 48 and 50 °C and 
C230 in BHI-broth at 45 and 50 °C and T100 in BHI at 45 and 52 °C and in Mornay sauce at 45, 48 
and 50 °C. All three strains showed growth in asparagus soup at 45 °C.   
This study concluded, that hot-holding temperatures should not be below 65 °C as Bacillus cereus 
sensu lato spores germinate at temperatures up to 52 °C.  
==PAGE:68==
DTU	  National	  Food	  Institute	  Research	  Group	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  s093510	  Mehtap	  Polat	  Akyol	  	  
for	  Microbiology	  and	  Hygiene	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  Master	  Thesis	  in	  Food	  Technology	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	      
	  
	  
	  
67	    
The experiment work in challenge tests obtained growth of Bacillus cereus sensu lato within three-
hour incubation, which showed that hot-holding of liquid foods should not exceed two hours. Based 
on the experiments performed, growth was not achieved at 54 °C in BHI-broth in 24 h, therefore it 
is necessary to hot hold foods above 54 °C to avoid active growth of the bacteria, that can cause 
foodborne disease.

CHEMICALS 
Make a list of the used Chemicals. 
Blood agar, BA-plates (BA, Oxoid, England)  
Tryptic soya agar, TSA-plates (TSA, Oxoid, England) ± 5 % sheep blood  
Brain Heart Infusion (BHI) broth, Oxoid  
Ethanol wipes  
Sporicidal wipes  
And the chemical residue that may be in the things we touch  
SUBSTANTIAL RISK FROM THE CHEMICIALS 
Only the most toxic chemicals – the chemicals toxic property - ex.  – Toxic if inhaled, carcinogenic 
in contact with skin or flammable. If there is used more than what is ordinary used, then state the 
amount used in this process. 
Blood agar:  
Suspected: Cutaneous Disease E.g. Dermatitis and Inhalation Allergy e.g. Asthma  
Toxicological information:  
Inhalation: May cause irritation to the mucous membranes in the upper respiratory tract.  
Inhalation-long: May cause inhalation allergy.  
Skin-acute: May cause irritation.  
Skin-long: May cause contact allergy.  
Eyes: May cause irritation.  
 
Tryptone Soya Agar:  
Ingestion: Causes irritation to the mucosa of the gastrointestinal tract.  
Nausea, vomiting, diarrhea.  
Precautions: 
In case of unavoidable skin contact, use disposable gloves.  
Eye wash bottles and sink with soap must be easily accessible. 
No information on the harmful effects of the substance.  
BIOLOGICAL AGENTS  
Ex. What bacteria and virus strains are used in the process? 
Bacillus Cereus sensu lato strains: 21750, 21792, 21800, 16238, 10329, 11129, 21803, 21791, 
T101, T100, 17544, 17533, T185, T183, T126, T147, Tomato, C261, C230, 21793 
 
SUBSTANTIAL RISK FROM THE BIOLOGICAL AGENTS & THE WORK PRO-
CESSES. 
Ex. Risk of infection, sample matrix, scalpels, centrifuge, vacuum or air pressure work etc. 
It is important to avoid transmission to the clothes and shoes

NECESSARY SAFETY PRECAUTION 
Ventilation 
Are the mentioned precaution necessary throughout the work process 
or only in parts of the process: 
Use Fume Hood when making agar or using centrifuge 
 Special gloves   
 
Which kind: Nitrite  
Are the mentioned gloves necessary throughout the work process or 
only in parts of the process:  
Gloves (nitrite) are necessary when using Ethanol wipes to wipe 
the table and when working with PCR  
Personal protective 
equipment (PPE) 
Lab coat: is necessary throughout the work process  
Goggles: No  
Respirator and brand of filter: No  
Special footwear: No 
Gloves: No 
Other precautionary 
Measurement 
Specifik heat source in a fire hazard: Yes  
Specific emergency  
equipment:  
Special fire-fighting equipment: Yes  
Specific training or 
instruction: 
 
Mandatory training, which: safety introduction before starting the 
lab-work  
Need instruction in how to operate a specific hazardous equipment, 
which: PCR 
Other: 
Safety precaution in re-
gards to biological agents. 
Do there occur any sharp objects in the work process?  
Which: Knife and scissors  
Do the work process form aerosols? Which precautions are set in 
place? 
 Bacillus cereus can form aerosols by plating 
__________________________________ 
 
 
WHATH TO DO IN AN EMERGENCY AND A SPILLAGE SITUATION? 
Note here what to do in a relevant accident, how to collect and dispose of spillage, procedure for 
notification in an emergency. 
It is important to use sprit and special cloth to remove a spillage of Bacillus cereus spores  
CHEMICAL AND INFECTIOUAS WASTE 
Note here what waste category the chemicals belong to, and how to handle biological waste. 
Biological waste must come in a yellow bag and be thrown out in the red box outside the lab  
EXPECTING A CHILD OR NURSING 
If you are pregnant or nursing please check the safety instruction on the Portalen. 
Pregnant women should stay away from the laboratories working with Listeria 
PROPOSAL FOR HOW TO IMPROVE THE SAFETY: 
Here you can give your input to the APV for the entire Institute/department.

Appendix 3: Calculations of salt content  
 
Asparagus soup:  
Salt- in- water (%) = 100 x ((salt pr. 100 g)/ (water pr. 100 g + salt pr. 100 g)) 
Fat/g + Carbohydrate/g +Protein/g = 1.3 g+ 3.7 g+ 0.8 g = 5.8 g  
100 g- 5.8 g= 94.2 g water  
Salt- in- water (%) = 100 x ((0.66 g salt pr. 100 g) / (94.2 g water pr. 100 g + 0.66 g salt pr. 100 g)) 
Salt in-water (%) = 0.7 %  
Mornay sauce:  
 
Salt- in- water (%) = 100 x ((salt pr. 100 g) / (water pr. 100 g + salt pr. 100 g)) 
Fat/g + Carbohydrate/g +Protein/g = 8.5 g+ 7.5 g+ 5.1 g = 21.7 g  
100 g- 21.7 g= 78. 3 g water  
Salt- in- water (%) = 100 x ((1,4 g salt pr. 100 g) / (78. 3 g water pr. 100 g + 1.4 g salt pr. 100 g)) 
Salt in-water (%) = 1.75 %

Figure	  26:	  The	  presence	  of	  the	  two	  enterotoxic	  genes	  (nheA	  and	  cytK)	  was	  detected	  by	  PCR	  in	  all	  Bacillus	  cereus	  strains.	  Of	  all	  19	  
strains	  were	  positive	  for	  nheA	  (750	  bp)	  strains,	  and	  one	  of	  them,	  17544	  was	  negative	  (Table	  47).	  Eight	  strains	  were	  detected	  positive	  
for	  the	  cytK	  gene	  (881	  bp)	  such	  as	  T100,	  21750,	  21791,	  16238,	  Tomato,	  T101,	  and	  21803),	  which	  are	  placed	  in	  row	  2	  on	  the	  gel	  elec-­‐
trophoresis.	  	  
Table	  46:	  All	  20	  Bacillus	  cereus	  strains	  tested	  for	  the	  nheA	  gene	  (750	  bp)	  were	  detected	  positive	  except	  the	  strain	  17544.	  The	  other	  
toxin	  gene	  cytK	  (881	  bp)	  that	  were	  investigated	  for	  the	  enterotoxin	  genes,	  which	  may	  be	  in	  the	  Bacillus	  cereus	  strains,	  showed	  
11129,	  T100,	  21750,	  21791,	  16238,	  Tomato,	  T101,	  and	  21803	  were	  positive	  for	  presence	  of	  the	  gene.	  Because	  of	  the	  limited	  place	  in	  
the	  gel	  electrophoresis,	  the	  samples	  were	  divided	  into	  two.	  In	  figure	  30,	  the	  results	  for	  the	  other	  four	  strains	  (T185,	  21793,	  17533,	  
and	  10329)	  are	  presented.

ble 19.
